GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*(T - c7)*sin(epsilon)
Candidate formulas: 67

GT (fixed) can be rewritten to expose its functional structure:
\[
\text{GT}=
99.7283\,\epsilon\big(1-0.0897644(T-330.5998)\big)\;+\;4.81853\,\epsilon^3\;+\;5.41674\,(T-330.5998)\sin(\epsilon).
\]
Expand the first term:
\[
99.7283\,\epsilon\;-\;(99.7283\cdot 0.0897644)\,\epsilon\,(T-330.5998).
\]
So GT is exactly a sum of these basis behaviors:
- an \(\epsilon\) term,
- an \(\epsilon(T-330.5998)\) term (i.e., bilinear in \(T\) and \(\epsilon\), plus a constant shift in \(T\)),
- an \(\epsilon^3\) term,
- a \((T-330.5998)\sin(\epsilon)\) term (i.e., \(T\sin(\epsilon)\) plus a constant\(\cdot\sin(\epsilon)\) piece).

Any matching candidate must be able to produce **both** (i) an \(\epsilon T\) bilinear term and (ii) a \(T\sin(\epsilon)\) term, while also producing \(\epsilon^3\) and \(\epsilon\), and **must not** introduce extra functional dependence (like \(e^{T}\), \(\log\), \(1/(a+bT)\), etc.) unless its coefficient can be set to 0.
